name: codex-required
# Per polaris-restart Plan section 10.1 + section 10.0 Codex isolation invariant.
# Required-status-check that gates `gh pr merge` for `bot/<issue_id>` PRs.
# Verifies the full §3.0 5-artifact triple is present and BOTH Codex
# verdicts (brief + diff) end with `verdict: APPROVE` as the FINAL verdict
# (not an arbitrary transcript line).
#
# Hardening notes (per PR-D iter 2 fixes):
# - PR-controlled head ref is passed via `env:` and validated against a
#   narrow safe regex BEFORE being used in bash; never interpolated as
#   `${{ ... }}` directly into shell source (PRD2-P1-002, P1-003).
# - Verdict files must declare a final verdict block at the END of the
#   artifact (PRD2-P1-001) so transcript prompt text containing the literal
#   string "verdict: APPROVE" cannot fool the gate. The convention is:
#   the LAST `verdict: APPROVE` or `verdict: REQUEST_CHANGES` line in the
#   file is treated as authoritative.
#
# Phase-2 hardening (post-PR-F, separate work): self-hosted runner with
# mounted `~/.codex/auth.json` so `codex exec` runs ON THE RUNNER per
# §10.0 line 898. Until then, this workflow parses verdict files committed
# by Claude; user reads `git log` morning per §7.B B1 as after-the-fact
# review surface.

on:
  pull_request:
    branches: [polaris, main]
    types: [opened, synchronize, reopened]

permissions:
  contents: read
  pull-requests: read

jobs:
  codex-required:
    runs-on: ubuntu-latest
    env:
      # PR-D iter 2 PRD2-P1-002 fix: PR-controlled value passed via env,
      # not interpolated directly into shell source. Branch names can
      # contain `$()`, quotes, semicolons, etc.
      HEAD_REF: ${{ github.event.pull_request.head.ref }}
    steps:
      - uses: actions/checkout@v4
        with:
          # PR-D iter 3 PRD3-P1-001 fix: full history needed for `git diff
          # base...head` to compute canonical PR diff and bind to
          # codex_diff.patch.
          fetch-depth: 0

      - name: extract_and_validate_issue_id
        id: issue
        run: |
          set -euo pipefail
          # Bot-PR head refs follow `bot/<issue_id>` per plan §3.0 + §7.A
          # LOCKED A2. Cleanup-PR-* and other infrastructure PRs are not
          # gated by codex-required (they have their own review trail).
          #
          # PR-D iter 2 PRD2-P1-002 fix: read $HEAD_REF from env, validate
          # against a narrow safe regex, reject if it doesn't match.
          # PR-D iter 3 PRD3-P2-002 fix: tightened regex to canonical
          # issue_breakdown.md schema `^I-[a-z0-9]{2,8}-[0-9]{3}`.
          # PR-D iter 4 PRD4-P1-001 fix: capture ONLY the base issue ID
          # (group 1). Optional descriptive slug after `-<NAME>` is
          # accepted in the head ref but DROPPED from issue_id, because
          # issue_breakdown.md §3 + §35 require the literal base ID for
          # artifact paths (e.g. `.codex/I-f1-001/`, NOT
          # `.codex/I-f1-001-scope-discovery/`).
          # PR-D iter 5 PRD5-P1-001 + iter 6 PRD6-P1-001 fix: explicit
          # infra-branch allowlist with EXACT enumeration of canonical
          # restart-sequence + cleanup-PR ids. PR-D itself
          # (`bot/pr-d-mechanical-gates`) and other infra branches SKIP
          # the gate cleanly. Only canonical `bot/I-...` issue branches
          # are gated.
          # Examples that SKIP: `bot/pr-d-mechanical-gates`,
          # `bot/cleanup-pr-3a-archive-m1m26`, `bot/pr-e`.
          # Examples that GATE: `bot/I-f1-001`, `bot/I-f1-001-scope-discovery`,
          # `bot/I-bug-079`, `bot/I-hand-003-final` -> issue_id =
          # `I-f1-001`, `I-bug-079`, `I-hand-003`.
          # Examples that REJECT (closed: branch-name bypass): `bot/pr-malicious`,
          # `bot/setup-anything`, `bot/slice-foo`, `bot/cleanup-pr-9` (no canonical PR-9).
          if [[ "$HEAD_REF" =~ ^bot/(I-[a-z0-9]{2,8}-[0-9]{3})(-[a-z0-9_-]+)?$ ]]; then
            issue_id="${BASH_REMATCH[1]}"
            printf 'issue_id=%s\n' "$issue_id" >> "$GITHUB_OUTPUT"
            printf 'skip=false\n' >> "$GITHUB_OUTPUT"
            echo "Validated bot-PR head ref: $HEAD_REF -> issue_id=$issue_id"
          elif [[ "$HEAD_REF" =~ ^bot/(pr-(a|a2|a3|b|b2|c|d|e|f)|cleanup-pr-(1|2|3a|3b|3c|4|5|6|7|8))(-[a-z0-9_-]+)?$ ]]; then
            # PR-D iter 6 PRD6-P1-001 fix: infra allowlist NARROWED to
            # exact known PR letters / cleanup PR ids. Branch name bypass
            # closed: `bot/pr-malicious`, `bot/setup-anything`, `bot/slice-foo`
            # all FAIL CLOSED to the catch-all reject below.
            #
            # Infrastructure branches enumerated explicitly (per PR-A..PR-F
            # restart sequence + Cleanup-PR-1..8 canonical 10-PR table):
            #   - bot/pr-a, bot/pr-a2, bot/pr-a3 (restart plan, issue_breakdown, cleanup_audit)
            #   - bot/pr-b, bot/pr-b2 (DNA doc substrate, polaris-controls relocation)
            #   - bot/pr-c (cleanup execution wrapper)
            #   - bot/pr-d (this PR — mechanical gates)
            #   - bot/pr-e (open all GitHub Issues)
            #   - bot/pr-f (execute Issue #1 — bridge to issue-driven flow)
            #   - bot/cleanup-pr-1..8 (with 3a/3b/3c sub-PRs per iter-17 split)
            #
            # Optional descriptive `-<slug>` suffix accepted (e.g.
            # `bot/pr-d-mechanical-gates`, `bot/cleanup-pr-3a-archive-m1m26`)
            # but does not change the allowlist match.
            #
            # These infra branches follow their own review protocol (Codex
            # review per their own brief like
            # `.codex/pr_d_mechanical_gates_review_brief.md`, NOT the §3.0
            # 5-artifact triple). Skip the codex-required gate.
            echo "Infrastructure bot branch '$HEAD_REF' (PR-A..F or Cleanup-PR-1..8); skipping codex-required gate"
            echo "       (review trail in .codex/<pr-name>_review_brief.md per PR-D iter 5/6 fix)"
            printf 'issue_id=\n' >> "$GITHUB_OUTPUT"
            printf 'skip=true\n' >> "$GITHUB_OUTPUT"
            printf 'infra_branch=true\n' >> "$GITHUB_OUTPUT"
          elif [[ "$HEAD_REF" == bot/* ]]; then
            # Starts with bot/ but doesn't match canonical issue_id schema
            # AND doesn't match the infra-branch allowlist. Reject explicitly
            # to prevent malformed issue IDs sneaking through the gate.
            echo "ERROR: head ref '$HEAD_REF' starts with bot/ but doesn't match"
            echo "       (a) canonical issue schema 'I-[a-z0-9]{2,8}-[0-9]{3}[-<NAME>]'"
            echo "           (per state/polaris_restart/issue_breakdown.md §3)"
            echo "       OR (b) infra allowlist: bot/pr-(a|a2|a3|b|b2|c|d|e|f) or"
            echo "          bot/cleanup-pr-(1|2|3a|3b|3c|4|5|6|7|8) [with optional -<slug>]"
            echo "       Use one of the allowed branch-name patterns."
            exit 1
          else
            echo "Non-bot PR (head ref does not start with bot/); skipping codex-required gate"
            printf 'issue_id=\n' >> "$GITHUB_OUTPUT"
            printf 'skip=true\n' >> "$GITHUB_OUTPUT"
          fi

      - name: verify_codex_artifacts
        if: steps.issue.outputs.skip != 'true'
        env:
          ISSUE_ID: ${{ steps.issue.outputs.issue_id }}
          BASE_SHA: ${{ github.event.pull_request.base.sha }}
          HEAD_SHA: ${{ github.event.pull_request.head.sha }}
        # PR-D iter 1 P1-001 fix: require the FULL 5-artifact triple per
        # CLAUDE.md §3.0 mandatory contract.
        # PR-D iter 2 PRD2-P1-001 fix: parse the FINAL verdict line in
        # each verdict file, not any matching line. Codex verdict
        # transcripts include prompt text that may itself contain the
        # literal string "verdict: APPROVE" (e.g., the brief schema block).
        # The LAST verdict-line in the file is authoritative.
        # PR-D iter 2 PRD2-P1-002 fix: ISSUE_ID also passed via env, validated
        # by upstream regex; safe to use in pathspecs.
        # PR-D iter 3 PRD3-P1-001 fix: BIND `codex_diff.patch` to the
        # actual PR diff via sha256. Compute canonical PR diff (excluding
        # review-artifact paths the gate itself accepts), hash it, and
        # require codex_diff.patch to declare the matching hash via a
        # `# canonical-diff-sha256: <64-hex>` trailer line. Without this
        # binding, Codex APPROVE on codex_diff.patch could cover code
        # different from what the PR actually contains.
        run: |
          set -euo pipefail
          BRIEF=".codex/${ISSUE_ID}/brief.md"
          BRIEF_VERDICT=".codex/${ISSUE_ID}/codex_brief_verdict.txt"
          DIFF_PATCH=".codex/${ISSUE_ID}/codex_diff.patch"
          DIFF_VERDICT=".codex/${ISSUE_ID}/codex_diff_audit.txt"
          CLAUDE_AUDIT="outputs/audits/${ISSUE_ID}/claude_audit.md"

          missing=0
          for f in "$BRIEF" "$BRIEF_VERDICT" "$DIFF_PATCH" "$DIFF_VERDICT" "$CLAUDE_AUDIT"; do
            if [ ! -f "$f" ]; then
              echo "ERROR: missing $f (CLAUDE.md §3.0 5-artifact triple)"
              missing=1
            fi
          done
          if [ "$missing" = "1" ]; then
            exit 1
          fi

          # Parse FINAL verdict line (last `verdict: ...` line in file).
          # Plan §7.C LOCKED C2: APPROVE means zero P0 AND zero P1.
          # `grep` returns the last match via `tail -1`; `[[ "$x" = "verdict: APPROVE" ]]`
          # ensures exact equality (not substring).
          check_final_verdict() {
            local file="$1"
            local label="$2"
            local final
            final="$(grep -E '^verdict:[[:space:]]+(APPROVE|REQUEST_CHANGES)$' "$file" | tail -1 || true)"
            if [ -z "$final" ]; then
              echo "ERROR: $label ($file) contains no final verdict line ('verdict: APPROVE' or 'verdict: REQUEST_CHANGES')"
              return 1
            fi
            if [ "$final" != "verdict: APPROVE" ]; then
              echo "ERROR: $label ($file) final verdict is NOT APPROVE: $final"
              return 1
            fi
            echo "OK: $label final verdict APPROVE"
          }

          check_final_verdict "$BRIEF_VERDICT" "brief"
          check_final_verdict "$DIFF_VERDICT" "diff"

          # PR-D iter 3 PRD3-P1-001 fix: bind codex_diff.patch to actual
          # PR diff. Compute canonical PR diff EXCLUDING review-artifact
          # paths (those are part of the PR but NOT what Codex reviewed
          # as the "code change"):
          #   - .codex/<ISSUE_ID>/**       (brief, verdicts, diff patch, audit)
          #   - outputs/audits/<ISSUE_ID>/** (claude audit)
          # Everything else in `git diff base...head` IS the code change
          # Codex reviewed and must match the codex_diff.patch hash.
          echo "Computing canonical PR diff base=$BASE_SHA head=$HEAD_SHA"
          canonical_diff="$(mktemp)"
          git diff "${BASE_SHA}...${HEAD_SHA}" -- \
            ":(exclude).codex/${ISSUE_ID}/" \
            ":(exclude)outputs/audits/${ISSUE_ID}/" \
            > "$canonical_diff"

          actual_hash="$(sha256sum "$canonical_diff" | awk '{print $1}')"
          echo "Canonical PR diff sha256: $actual_hash"

          # Codex-approved diff must declare its canonical hash via a
          # trailer line `# canonical-diff-sha256: <64-hex>` ANYWHERE in
          # codex_diff.patch. Convention: Claude appends this line as a
          # patch comment after running `sha256sum` on the same canonical
          # diff right before submitting to Codex review. The hash binds
          # the Codex APPROVE to one specific code change.
          declared_hash="$(grep -E '^# canonical-diff-sha256: [a-f0-9]{64}$' "$DIFF_PATCH" | tail -1 | awk '{print $3}' || true)"
          if [ -z "$declared_hash" ]; then
            echo "ERROR: $DIFF_PATCH has no '# canonical-diff-sha256: <64-hex>' trailer line"
            echo "       Required by PR-D iter 3 PRD3-P1-001 fix to bind Codex APPROVE"
            echo "       to a specific code change (otherwise approved patch and actual"
            echo "       PR diff can diverge silently)."
            exit 1
          fi

          if [ "$actual_hash" != "$declared_hash" ]; then
            echo "ERROR: PR diff hash mismatch — codex_diff.patch was approved for a"
            echo "       different code change than the actual PR contains."
            echo "  declared (in codex_diff.patch trailer): $declared_hash"
            echo "  actual (current canonical PR diff):     $actual_hash"
            echo "Either re-run Codex review on the current PR diff and update the"
            echo "trailer with the new hash, or revert the un-reviewed code changes."
            exit 1
          fi

          echo "OK: 5-artifact triple present, both Codex final verdicts APPROVE,"
          echo "    and codex_diff.patch hash matches actual PR diff for $ISSUE_ID"

      - name: skip_summary
        if: steps.issue.outputs.skip == 'true'
        env:
          IS_INFRA: ${{ steps.issue.outputs.infra_branch }}
          HEAD_REF_FOR_LOG: ${{ github.event.pull_request.head.ref }}
        # PR-D iter 6 PRD6-P2-001 fix: distinguish infra-branch skip from
        # non-bot skip in audit log. Earlier wording always said "PR head
        # ref does not start with bot/" even when an infra bot/* branch
        # had matched the allowlist.
        run: |
          if [ "${IS_INFRA:-false}" = "true" ]; then
            echo "codex-required: skipped (infra branch '$HEAD_REF_FOR_LOG' on PR-A..F or Cleanup-PR-1..8 allowlist; uses its own review trail in .codex/<pr-name>_review_brief.md)"
          else
            echo "codex-required: skipped (non-bot PR head ref '$HEAD_REF_FOR_LOG'; not gated by §3.0 issue-driven workflow)"
          fi

exec

 GCC RUNTIME LIBRARY EXCEPTION

 Version 3.1, 31 March 2009

 Copyright (C) 2009 Free Software Foundation, Inc. <http://fsf.org/>

 Everyone is permitted to copy and distribute verbatim copies of this
 license document, but changing it is not allowed.

 This GCC Runtime Library Exception ("Exception") is an additional
 permission under section 7 of the GNU General Public License, version
 3 ("GPLv3"). It applies to a given file (the "Runtime Library") that
 bears a notice placed by the copyright holder of the file stating that
 the file is governed by GPLv3 along with this Exception.

 When you use GCC to compile a program, GCC may combine portions of
 certain GCC header files and runtime libraries with the compiled
 program. The purpose of this Exception is to allow compilation of
 non-GPL (including proprietary) programs to use, in this way, the
 header files and runtime libraries covered by this Exception.

 0. Definitions.

 A file is an "Independent Module" if it either requires the Runtime
 Library for execution after a Compilation Process, or makes use of an
 interface provided by the Runtime Library, but is not otherwise based
 on the Runtime Library.

 "GCC" means a version of the GNU Compiler Collection, with or without
 modifications, governed by version 3 (or a specified later version) of
 the GNU General Public License (GPL) with the option of using any
 subsequent versions published by the FSF.

 "GPL-compatible Software" is software whose conditions of propagation,
 modification and use would permit combination with GCC in accord with
 the license of GCC.

 "Target Code" refers to output from any compiler for a real or virtual
 target processor architecture, in executable form or suitable for
 input to an assembler, loader, linker and/or execution
 phase. Notwithstanding that, Target Code does not include data in any
 format that is used as a compiler intermediate representation, or used
 for producing a compiler intermediate representation.

 The "Compilation Process" transforms code entirely represented in
 non-intermediate languages designed for human-written code, and/or in
 Java Virtual Machine byte code, into Target Code. Thus, for example,
 use of source code generators and preprocessors need not be considered
 part of the Compilation Process, since the Compilation Process can be
 understood as starting with the output of the generators or
 preprocessors.

 A Compilation Process is "Eligible" if it is done using GCC, alone or
 with other GPL-compatible software, or if it is done without using any
 work based on GCC. For example, using non-GPL-compatible Software to
 optimize any GCC intermediate representations would not qualify as an
 Eligible Compilation Process.

 1. Grant of Additional Permission.

 You have permission to propagate a work of Target Code formed by
 combining the Runtime Library with Independent Modules, even if such
 propagation would otherwise violate the terms of GPLv3, provided that
 all Target Code was generated by Eligible Compilation Processes. You
 may then convey such a combination under terms of your choice,
 consistent with the licensing of the Independent Modules.

 2. No Weakening of GCC Copyleft.

 The availability of this Exception does not imply any general
 presumption that third-party software is unaffected by the copyleft
 requirements of the license of GCC.

 This GCC Runtime Library Exception ("Exception") is an additional

 3 ("GPLv3"). It applies to a given file (the "Runtime Library") that
 bears a notice placed by the copyright holder of the file stating that
 the file is governed by GPLv3 along with this Exception.

 When you use GCC to compile a program, GCC may combine portions of
 certain GCC header files and runtime libraries with the compiled
 program. The purpose of this Exception is to allow compilation of
 non-GPL (including proprietary) programs to use, in this way, the
 header files and runtime libraries covered by this Exception.

 0. Definitions.

 A file is an "Independent Module" if it either requires the Runtime
 Library for execution after a Compilation Process, or makes use of an
 interface provided by the Runtime Library, but is not otherwise based
 on the Runtime Library.

 "GCC" means a version of the GNU Compiler Collection, with or without
 modifications, governed by version 3 (or a specified later version) of
 the GNU General Public License (GPL) with the option of using any
 subsequent versions published by the FSF.

 "GPL-compatible Software" is software whose conditions of propagation,
 modification and use would permit combination with GCC in accord with
 the license of GCC.

 "Target Code" refers to output from any compiler for a real or virtual
 target processor architecture, in executable form or suitable for
 input to an assembler, loader, linker and/or execution
 phase. Notwithstanding that, Target Code does not include data in any
 format that is used as a compiler intermediate representation, or used
 for producing a compiler intermediate representation.

 The "Compilation Process" transforms code entirely represented in
 non-intermediate languages designed for human-written code, and/or in
 Java Virtual Machine byte code, into Target Code. Thus, for example,
 use of source code generators and preprocessors need not be considered
 part of the Compilation Process, since the Compilation Process can be
 understood as starting with the output of the generators or
 preprocessors.

 A Compilation Process is "Eligible" if it is done using GCC, alone or
 with other GPL-compatible software, or if it is done without using any
 work based on GCC. For example, using non-GPL-compatible Software to
 optimize any GCC intermediate representations would not qualify as an
 Eligible Compilation Process.

 consistent with the licensing of the Independent Modules.

   1: """HDBSCAN clustering on top-K retrieval candidate embeddings (F2 substrate).
   2: 
   3: Per Carney v6.2 §F2 Diversify-then-Verify: cluster the top-K candidate
   4: embeddings; if HDBSCAN finds more than one dense cluster the user query
   5: is ambiguous (e.g. "BPEI" → syndrome / institute / chemical clusters),
   6: and the disambiguation modal should fire. A single dense cluster (or
   7: one-cluster-allowed result) means the query is unambiguous (e.g.
   8: "tirzepatide" → all candidates about the drug).
   9: 
  10: This module is substrate-only:
  11: - Consumes pre-computed `np.ndarray` of shape (K, D); does NOT call
  12:   any embedding model at runtime (per CLAUDE.md §8.4 "no heavy ML in
  13:   autonomous loops"). Wiring into `live_retriever.py` is I-f2-003.
  14: - Wraps `hdbscan.HDBSCAN` with `allow_single_cluster=True` so a
  15:   tightly-packed candidate set returns 1 cluster rather than 0.
  16: 
  17: Pre-condition: `embeddings` should be L2-normalized for euclidean
  18: metric to be monotonic with cosine distance.
  19: """
  20: 
  21: from __future__ import annotations
  22: 
  23: from dataclasses import dataclass
  24: 
  25: import hdbscan
  26: import numpy as np
  27: 
  28: 
  29: @dataclass(frozen=True)
  30: class ClusterResult:
  31:     """Result of HDBSCAN clustering on candidate embeddings.
  32: 
  33:     Attributes:
  34:         labels: HDBSCAN cluster id per candidate (-1 = noise/outlier).
  35:         num_clusters: Count of distinct non-noise cluster ids.
  36:         is_ambiguous: True iff num_clusters > 1.
  37:     """
  38: 
  39:     labels: list[int]
  40:     num_clusters: int
  41:     is_ambiguous: bool
  42: 
  43: 
  44: def cluster_candidates(
  45:     embeddings: np.ndarray,
  46:     min_cluster_size: int = 2,
  47: ) -> ClusterResult:
  48:     """Cluster candidate embeddings with HDBSCAN.
  49: 
  50:     Args:
  51:         embeddings: Shape (K, D) float array of candidate embeddings.
  52:         min_cluster_size: HDBSCAN minimum cluster size (default 2 per
  53:             Carney v6.2 §F2 spec).
  54: 
  55:     Returns:
  56:         ClusterResult with labels, num_clusters, is_ambiguous.
  57: 
  58:     Raises:
  59:         ValueError: If `embeddings` is empty (LAW II — fail loudly).
  60: 
  61:     Edge cases:
  62:         - K < min_cluster_size: HDBSCAN cannot cluster; returns
  63:           num_clusters=0, is_ambiguous=False, labels all -1.
  64:     """
  65:     if embeddings.size == 0:
  66:         raise ValueError(
  67:             "cluster_candidates: empty embedding array; cannot cluster"
  68:         )
  69: 
  70:     n_candidates = embeddings.shape[0]
  71:     if n_candidates < min_cluster_size:
  72:         return ClusterResult(
  73:             labels=[-1] * n_candidates,
  74:             num_clusters=0,
  75:             is_ambiguous=False,
  76:         )
  77: 
  78:     clusterer = hdbscan.HDBSCAN(
  79:         min_cluster_size=min_cluster_size,
  80:         metric="euclidean",
  81:         allow_single_cluster=True,
  82:     )
  83:     raw_labels = clusterer.fit_predict(embeddings)
  84:     labels = [int(label) for label in raw_labels]
  85:     distinct_clusters = set(labels) - {-1}
  86:     num_clusters = len(distinct_clusters)
  87:     return ClusterResult(
  88:         labels=labels,
  89:         num_clusters=num_clusters,
  90:         is_ambiguous=num_clusters > 1,
  91:     )

   1: """Unit tests for I-f2-001 — HDBSCAN clustering substrate.
   2: 
   3: Synthetic numpy embeddings only (no real embedding model load) per
   4: CLAUDE.md §8.4: heavy ML is forbidden in autonomous loops.
   5: """
   6: 
   7: from __future__ import annotations
   8: 
   9: import numpy as np
  10: import pytest
  11: 
  12: from polaris_graph.intake.disambiguation_clusterer import (
  13:     ClusterResult,
  14:     cluster_candidates,
  15: )
  16: 
  17: 
  18: def _gaussian_cloud(rng: np.random.Generator, center: tuple[float, ...], n: int, scale: float = 0.05) -> np.ndarray:
  19:     """Make `n` points centered at `center` with small Gaussian noise."""
  20:     centroid = np.array(center, dtype=np.float64)
  21:     noise = rng.normal(loc=0.0, scale=scale, size=(n, len(center)))
  22:     return centroid + noise
  23: 
  24: 
  25: def test_three_clear_clusters_ambiguous() -> None:
  26:     rng = np.random.default_rng(seed=42)
  27:     cloud_a = _gaussian_cloud(rng, (0.0, 0.0), 5)
  28:     cloud_b = _gaussian_cloud(rng, (10.0, 10.0), 5)
  29:     cloud_c = _gaussian_cloud(rng, (-10.0, -10.0), 5)
  30:     embeddings = np.vstack([cloud_a, cloud_b, cloud_c])
  31: 
  32:     result = cluster_candidates(embeddings)
  33: 
  34:     assert isinstance(result, ClusterResult)
  35:     assert result.num_clusters == 3
  36:     assert result.is_ambiguous is True
  37: 
  38: 
  39: def test_single_dense_cluster_unambiguous() -> None:
  40:     rng = np.random.default_rng(seed=7)
  41:     embeddings = _gaussian_cloud(rng, (0.0, 0.0), 10)
  42: 
  43:     result = cluster_candidates(embeddings)
  44: 
  45:     assert result.num_clusters == 1
  46:     assert result.is_ambiguous is False
  47: 
  48: 
  49: def test_two_clusters_ambiguous() -> None:
  50:     rng = np.random.default_rng(seed=11)
  51:     cloud_a = _gaussian_cloud(rng, (0.0, 0.0), 5)
  52:     cloud_b = _gaussian_cloud(rng, (10.0, 10.0), 5)
  53:     embeddings = np.vstack([cloud_a, cloud_b])
  54: 
  55:     result = cluster_candidates(embeddings)
  56: 
  57:     assert result.num_clusters == 2
  58:     assert result.is_ambiguous is True
  59: 
  60: 
  61: def test_below_min_cluster_size_returns_noise() -> None:
  62:     embeddings = np.array([[0.5, 0.5]], dtype=np.float64)
  63: 
  64:     result = cluster_candidates(embeddings, min_cluster_size=2)
  65: 
  66:     assert result.num_clusters == 0
  67:     assert result.is_ambiguous is False
  68:     assert result.labels == [-1]
  69: 
  70: 
  71: def test_empty_input_raises() -> None:
  72:     embeddings = np.empty((0, 384), dtype=np.float64)
  73: 
  74:     with pytest.raises(ValueError, match="empty embedding array"):
  75:         cluster_candidates(embeddings)

# Codex Brief Review — I-f2-001 (ITER 2 of 5)

## Iter-1 fixes
- **P1: HDBSCAN default `allow_single_cluster=False`** — single-dense-cluster test would return `num_clusters=0` not `1`. Iter-2 fix: pass `allow_single_cluster=True` to HDBSCAN constructor. Per https://hdbscan.readthedocs.io/en/latest/api.html.
- **P2: hdbscan latest is 0.8.42 (Mar 2026), not 0.8.40.** Iter-2 fix: pin `hdbscan>=0.8.40,<0.9` (lower-bound 0.8.40 still safe; upper bound prevents accidental 0.9.x breakage). Wording corrected.

**HARD ITERATION CAP: 5 per document. This is iter 2 of 5.**
- Front-load ALL real findings in iter 1. No drip-feeding across iterations.
- Same quality bar regardless of iteration count.
- "Don't pick bone from egg" — if a finding isn't a real solid blocker, classify it as P3/P2/cosmetic; reserve P0/P1 for real execution risks.
- If iter 5 returns REQUEST_CHANGES, the document is force-APPROVE'd by Claude on remaining-non-P0/P1 findings; do not bank issues for iter 6.
- If you detect "I'm holding back a P1 to surface in the next round" — DON'T. Surface it now. The 5-cap means iter 6 doesn't exist; banked findings die at iter 5.
- Verdict APPROVE iff zero NOVEL P0 AND zero continuing P0 AND zero P1.

**Issue:** I-f2-001 — Backend: HDBSCAN clustering on top-K retrieval candidates
**Phase:** 1 / **Feature:** F2 (disambiguation modal)
**LOC budget:** 180 net per `state/polaris_restart/issue_breakdown.md`. **CHARTER §1 hard cap: 200.**

## Mission

Add `src/polaris_graph/intake/disambiguation_clusterer.py` — a pure-Python module that takes top-K candidate embeddings and returns HDBSCAN cluster labels. >1 cluster = ambiguous query (BPEI = syndrome / institute / chemical → 3 clusters). 1 dense cluster = unambiguous (tirzepatide → all candidates about the drug → 1 cluster).

Per Carney plan §F2: "Diversify-then-Verify pipeline (Agentic Verification, ICLR 2025); HDBSCAN clustering on candidate embeddings."

## Substrate (HONEST)

- `src/polaris_graph/intake/__init__.py` exists with `question_normalizer` (slice 001).
- `numpy>=1.24` already in `requirements.txt` (line 111). **`hdbscan` is NOT in requirements.txt.** Must add.
- `pooled_embedder.py` exists at `src/polaris_graph/retrieval/`; this Issue does NOT call it (test-isolated; consumes pre-computed embedding arrays).
- This Issue is substrate ONLY. Wiring into `live_retriever.py` is I-f2-003 scope.
- F2 substrate per Carney plan §F2 also flags spaCy NOT installed; this module does NOT need spaCy (operates on numeric embeddings only).

## Acceptance criteria (binding)

1. **`src/polaris_graph/intake/disambiguation_clusterer.py`** (NEW): exports `cluster_candidates(embeddings: np.ndarray, min_cluster_size: int = 2) -> ClusterResult` where:
   - `embeddings` is shape `(K, D)` array of floats (K candidates, D embedding dim).
   - Returns `ClusterResult` dataclass with `labels: list[int]` (HDBSCAN cluster id per candidate; -1 = noise/outlier per HDBSCAN convention), `num_clusters: int` (count of distinct non-noise labels), `is_ambiguous: bool` (= num_clusters > 1).
   - Wraps `hdbscan.HDBSCAN(min_cluster_size=min_cluster_size, metric="euclidean", allow_single_cluster=True)` from the `hdbscan` package. `allow_single_cluster=True` is required so a tightly-packed candidate set returns 1 cluster rather than 0 (P1-iter1 fix).
   - Edge case: K < min_cluster_size → `num_clusters=0`, `is_ambiguous=False`, all labels = -1 (no clustering possible). Document this in the docstring.
   - Edge case: empty input array → raises `ValueError` (LAW II — fail loudly).
   - LOC: ~70-90 (module + dataclass + docstring).

2. **`tests/polaris_graph/intake/test_disambiguation_clusterer.py`** (NEW): unit tests using **synthetic numpy arrays** (no real embedding model load — keeps test fast + GPU-free per CLAUDE.md §8.4 "no heavy ML in autonomous loops"):
   - `test_three_clear_clusters`: 3 well-separated point clouds (e.g. center [0,0], [10,10], [-10,-10] each ×5 with small Gaussian noise) → `num_clusters == 3`, `is_ambiguous == True`.
   - `test_single_dense_cluster`: 1 tight cloud of 10 points around [0,0] → `num_clusters == 1`, `is_ambiguous == False`.
   - `test_below_min_cluster_size`: 1 point → `num_clusters == 0`, `is_ambiguous == False`, labels `[-1]`.
   - `test_empty_input_raises`: `np.empty((0, 384))` → raises ValueError.
   - `test_two_clusters_ambiguous`: 2 separated point clouds → `num_clusters == 2`, `is_ambiguous == True`.
   - LOC: ~80.

3. **`requirements.txt`**: add `hdbscan>=0.8.40,<0.9` (stable Python 3.13-compatible range; latest 0.8.42 released Mar 2026 per pypi.org/project/hdbscan; pure-Python + C extension; no GPU dep).
   - Verify build works on Linux CI (hdbscan has C extensions; pip-install needs gcc — already present in `web_ci.yml` Python step).
   - LOC: +1.

## Out of scope (deferred per breakdown)

- LLM cluster-labeling (assigning "syndrome" / "institute" / "chemical" labels) → I-f2-002.
- Disambiguation API endpoint exposing cluster results → I-f2-003.
- Frontend modal → I-f2-004.

## Non-acceptance / explicit exclusions

- Does NOT call any embedding model at runtime (test-isolated; consumes pre-computed `np.ndarray`).
- Does NOT add spaCy or any NER tool.
- Does NOT depend on `pooled_embedder.py` (called by future Issue at integration time).
- Does NOT modify `live_retriever.py` (that's I-f2-003).
- Does NOT modify `question_normalizer.py`.

## Risks for Codex Red-Team

1. **`hdbscan` package install failures.** hdbscan 0.8.x ships C extensions (Cython); on Windows requires MSVC build tools, on Linux requires gcc. Both present in standard dev/CI environments. Pinned `>=0.8.40` is the latest stable per pypi.org/project/hdbscan as of 2026-05-06; this version supports Python 3.13. Verify the version constraint doesn't conflict with numpy>=1.24 already in requirements.

2. **`min_cluster_size=2` semantics.** HDBSCAN with `min_cluster_size=2` is unusually aggressive — it'll form clusters around any 2+ close points. The breakdown spec explicitly calls for `min_cluster_size=2` (default). Documented + asserted in tests.

3. **Noise-label convention (-1).** HDBSCAN labels outlier points as -1 (not part of any cluster). `num_clusters` excludes -1 from the count: `len(set(labels) - {-1})`. Edge case: ALL points are noise → `num_clusters == 0`, `is_ambiguous == False`. Acceptable.

4. **`euclidean` metric for normalized embeddings.** Most modern embedding models output L2-normalized vectors. Euclidean distance on normalized vectors is monotonic with cosine distance, so clustering quality is equivalent. Pre-condition documented in module docstring: "embeddings should be L2-normalized for best results."

5. **Synthetic test fixtures use `np.random.default_rng(seed)` for determinism.** Per CLAUDE.md §9.4, `np.random` is forbidden outside tests/fixtures/. Tests file explicitly sets seeded RNG within each test body — deterministic, reproducible, lint-clean for the LAW.

6. **Test must NOT load any real embedding model.** Per CLAUDE.md §8.4: "Heavy ML / vector / CUDA processes are forbidden in autonomous loops." Tests use synthetic numpy arrays only. No `sentence-transformers`, no `pooled_embedder` import.

7. **`tests/polaris_graph/intake/__init__.py`** — does it exist? Check before writing the test file. If not, create an empty `__init__.py` to make pytest discovery work. Adds 1 file but 0 LOC (empty marker).

import numpy as np
from polaris_graph.intake.disambiguation_clusterer import cluster_candidates
rng = np.random.default_rng(123)
centers = []
for i in range(3):
    c = np.zeros(384)
    c[i] = 10.0
    centers.append(c)
emb = np.vstack([c + rng.normal(0, 0.01, size=(5, 384)) for c in centers])
print(cluster_candidates(emb))
